  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });

  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25992189" rel="nofollow noopener">ACE #1</a>
</b><br /><br />After a Vampire Tracker Marks her with a crescent moon on her forehead, 16-year-old Zoey Redbird enters the House of Night and learns that she is no average fledgling. She has been Marked as special by the vampyre Goddess Nyx and has affinities for all five elements: Air, Fire Water, Earth and Spirit. But she is not the only fledgling at the House of Night with special powers. When she discovers that the leader of the Dark Daughters, the school’s most elite club, is mis-using her Goddess-given gifts, Zoey must look deep within herself for the courage to embrace her destiny – with a little help from her new vampyre friends (or Nerd Herd, as Aphrodite calls them)</span>
  <a data-text-id="10555376496252347124" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/367383-would-this-series-be-appropriate-to-put-in">Would this series be appropriate to put in my middle school library?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_367383'><a id="like_count_community_question_367383" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/367383?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">3 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F30183.Marked">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/367383-would-this-series-be-appropriate-to-put-in">5 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/367383-would-this-series-be-appropriate-to-put-in">See all 16 answers</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>

</div>
<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/66080201-elesse-w"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1509945980i/66080201._UX100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/66080201-elesse-w">Elesse W.</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Middle school, no. High school, yes. Yes there is brief swearing and sexual content here and there, but these kids are in high school. They're experie<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Middle school, no. High school, yes. Yes there is brief swearing and sexual content here and there, but these kids are in high school. They're experiencing these things already whether parents know it or not. I recommend it because there is MAJOR character development. A lot of lesson's learned. Honestly a character could either be relatable (because not every young adult is an angel) and show them what they may be doing wrong and what they should fix or change, or the character could be completely unrelatable but give young adults some insight and intelligence on things to look out for while in high school. I read this series from 8th grade til the last book came out after I graduated and to be perfectly completely honest, these books will make you think twice. <br />Example:<br />(Remember that time Zoey cheated on her boyfriend and broke his heart and in the end, it was definitely not worth it and a HUGE mistake.) <br />The way the characters grow and correct their mistakes is something I believe would be worth reading.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/181219701" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/181219701?book_show_action=true">Jul 01, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Haleema" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Haleema" href="/user/show/4336293-haleema">Haleema</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

           <span class="uitext reviewText">What is this? Recommend it to someone? NEVER!</span></div>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4336293-haleema?shelf=bad-writing">bad-writing</a>,

<span id="freeTextContainer11072468043935301551">Beware of spoilers! (But then again, just don't read this book.)<br/><br/>Warning: This review is just me being very <i>negative</i>. In no way will this review sound intelligent and well written. Therefore, if you wish to continue, you may.<br/><br/>Anyway, I will start all the way from the beginning. There are so many things I'd like to point out.<br/><br/>I pick up the book. I see the cover. It's a picture of half a girl's face. I'm guessing that's Zoey. Whatever. I look at the back. There is a comment from Gena Showalter on the</span>
  <span id="freeText11072468043935301551" style="display:none">Beware of spoilers! (But then again, just don't read this book.)<br><br>Warning: This review is just me being very <i>negative</i>. In no way will this review sound intelligent and well written. Therefore, if you wish to continue, you may.<br><br>Anyway, I will start all the way from the beginning. There are so many things I'd like to point out.<br><br>I pick up the book. I see the cover. It's a picture of half a girl's face. I'm guessing that's Zoey. Whatever. I look at the back. There is a comment from Gena Showalter on the top that says: <br><br>"From the moment I stuck my face in this book it hooked me! Totally awesome new take on vampires! Marked is hot and dark and funny. It rocks!" <br><br>First of all, what kind of author talks like that? Or is she just as idiotic as the Casts? Or maybe she really did like it. Or maybe the Casts "made her write that." Confused? You'll see what I'm talking about shortly. There is also a dreadfully long summary of the whole damn book on the back. Way to give away almost everything.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380352435ra/705890.gif" width="300" height="195" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>The Characters:</b> <br>Let's start with the protagonist herself, Zoey Redbird. <br><br>I found someone whinier than Bella Swan. Someone more stupid than Bella Swan. Someone more clumsy than Bella Swan. <br><br><b>Specific evidence of Zoey's stupidity:</b><br><br>- Page 1: "If I died, would it get me out of my geometry test tomorrow? One could only hope."<br><br>Oh, that's completely understandable. I mean, I feel dumb for thinking about whether I left a lasting legacy. I should be thinking about minuscule matters such as school tests. Silly me. <br><br>- Page 46: "She wasn't thin like the freak girls who puked and starved themselves into what they thought was Paris Hilton chic. ("That's hott." Yeah, okay, whatever, Paris.") <br><br>Freak girls? Because anorexia and bulimia are not serious issues at all... <br><br>Page 100: "Cereal?" I suddenly perked up. I seriously adore cereal, and have an I heart Cereal shirt somewhere to prove it." <br><br>Do I need to even explain what's wrong with that?<br><br>Page 188: "Can I ask you something? It's kinda personal," Erik said. "Hey you've seen me drink blood from a cup and like it, puke, kiss a guy, lick his blood like I'm a puppy, and then bawl my eyes out. And I've seen you turn down a blow job. I think I can manage to answer a kinda personal question." <br><br>What.<br><br>Page 277: "Aphrodite laughed a throaty, I'm-so-grown-up-and-you're-just-a-kid laugh. I really hate it when girls do that. I mean, yes, she's older, but I have boobs, too."<br><br>Yes, because only breasts signify that a girl is grown up. Great message, Casts.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/288945.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Also, I wanted to shoot myself with the stupid parenthetical overkill they put throughout the whole damn book.<br><br>I'm not sure if they deliberately created Zoey for the sole reason that we should all hate her. They have <i>no idea</i> how teenagers act and talk. Apparently all teenagers say LIKE OMG! NO WAY! YEAH, WHATEVER! I HAVE BOOBS, TOO! ZOMG.<br><br>Zoey is the special, one-of-a-kind, "chosen one." Only she can rule the world, basically. Her mentor is the best. She has all the powers. She is the one and only. Cliche much? Very. I was just sad I was stuck inside her head for the entire book. I felt suffocated.<br><br>Zoey's friends are all pathetic excuses for friends. The "twins" are annoying little brats. Damon is just a moron. And oh yeah, the country girl. Stevie Rae is just fucking annoying.<br><br>Aphrodite and Erik. I couldn't stop laughing every time I read about them. <br><br>AND WHO THE HELL HAS ORAL SEX IN THE MIDDLE OF A SCHOOL HALLWAY?! Or am I really that naive when it comes to horny high school children? <br><br>- Erik is the <s>more stupid</s> hotter version of Edward Cullen. He follows Zoey around. He asks her incredibly awkward/creepy questions. He's just very romantic, am I right.<br><br><b>Erik =</b> <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380352435ra/705893.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>That's the ugliest thing I've seen in my entire life.<br><br>- Aphrodite is just a poor excuse for an antagonist. *Googles Aphrodite* Oh! The Greek goddess of love, beauty, and sexuality! Another character whose name defines her personality. *rolls eyes*<br><br><b>The writing:</b> <br>I guess editing just lost its meaning in the midst of horrible books. Where is Editing?! Where are you, my love?!<br><br>I'm not even going to talk about the plot because there was no plot. I only read half the book (painfully), but I'm certain there was no plot for the parts I didn't read as well. <br><br>I know this is said very lightly sometimes, but this is actually the worst book I've ever read. It was so painful to accept that this was actually published.<br><br><b>I just want to say one last, important thing to the Casts:</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380352435i/705894.jpg" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer18306336561288185009">Read about half of it. Hated it. I'm returning the rest to the library.<br/><br/>The authors tried to make so many references to pop culture, they sounded ridiculous, and then were even proud of themselves for "sounding like teenagers," as they stated in the preface. Dumb. They tried to make moral lessons out of the life of this "fledgling," and had her reject things like Paris Hilton's weight, oral sex amongst teenagers, and Ashton Kutcher unfortunately liking older women. Oh, and the world was separated</span>
  <span id="freeText18306336561288185009" style="display:none">Read about half of it. Hated it. I'm returning the rest to the library.<br /><br />The authors tried to make so many references to pop culture, they sounded ridiculous, and then were even proud of themselves for "sounding like teenagers," as they stated in the preface. Dumb. They tried to make moral lessons out of the life of this "fledgling," and had her reject things like Paris Hilton's weight, oral sex amongst teenagers, and Ashton Kutcher unfortunately liking older women. Oh, and the world was separated into the "vampyres" and the religious right. Could they be more obviously parading their own moral agenda in young adult fiction? Regardless of whether you agree or disagree with the values they project in this book, they make it so plain that they are trying to jam-pack the book with certain ideals that it turns out like literary crap. If you want an awesome, captivating fantasy fiction series that gets teenage girls thinking about our over-sexualized and beautified culture, try Scott Westerfield. He's a little more subtle, and thus requires some intelligent thought on what you're reading. </span>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer105714015" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer11297120267634236077">This was how the book started. The first two pages literally went like this:<br/><br/>Tweeny 1: "ZOMG like -insert some teeny bs gossip here-"<br/><br/>Tweeny 2: "ZOMG like no! -more teeny gossip and more OMGs-"<br/><br/>Tweeny 1: "ZOMG like yeah."<br/><br/>All of a sudden some macho vamp guy stands in the hallway, points at teeny no #1 and is like "ZOEY YOU HAVE BEEN CHOSEN TO BE THE MAIN CHARACTER IN A BOOK THAT IS SO NOT TRYING TO BE LIKE TWILIGHT BUT YEAH YOU HAVE BEEN CHOSEN."<br/><br/>Then they're like "ZOMG YOU HAVE BEEN CHOSEN."<br/><br/>Tweeny 1</span>
  <span id="freeText11297120267634236077" style="display:none">This was how the book started. The first two pages literally went like this:<br /><br />Tweeny 1: "ZOMG like -insert some teeny bs gossip here-"<br /><br />Tweeny 2: "ZOMG like no! -more teeny gossip and more OMGs-"<br /><br />Tweeny 1: "ZOMG like yeah."<br /><br />All of a sudden some macho vamp guy stands in the hallway, points at teeny no #1 and is like "ZOEY YOU HAVE BEEN CHOSEN TO BE THE MAIN CHARACTER IN A BOOK THAT IS SO NOT TRYING TO BE LIKE TWILIGHT BUT YEAH YOU HAVE BEEN CHOSEN."<br /><br />Then they're like "ZOMG YOU HAVE BEEN CHOSEN."<br /><br />Tweeny 1: "SNAP. I have been chosen."<br /><br />Tweeny 2: "SNAP AND ZOMG YOU'RE A FREAK NOW I'M OUT OF HERE."<br /><br />And that, ladies and gentlemen, is how the worst book I have ever read starts off. Worse than Twilight, worse than Hush, hush, and worse than Evermore (almost). This book was just one big melodramatic teen angsty bitch fit. With vampyres. And stereotypes. And a sexy hunk. And a Queen Bee arch rival. And a blowjob. And of course the main character is a complete Mary sue, once again.<br /><br />I first read this just as a laugh, because sometimes I want to read bad books for the lolz. But what was at first fun to make fun of then turned horrifically bad, and eventually so intolerable that I had to close it halfway. As soon as Zoey was in love with Shakespeare vampire hunk, (sorry, vampYre) I just couldn't handle further stupidity. I could not believe this was written by two adults. This was like fanfiction. I have seen fanfiction which went along pretty much the same basis as this book. Heck I have seen fanfiction which was BETTER WRITTEN and BETTER OVERALL than this book. <br /><br />Zoey was absolutely frustrating and so easy to hate. That's horridly inconvenient since she's the main character, and we're being told this 'story' from her perspective. She whines and complains about EVERYTHING, and is an obvious attempt at a parody of a teenager by these two idiots of women authors. A pin would fall to the ground and immediately her life is oooooverrrrrr. Also according to Zoey, if you don't nail your underwear and your bra to your body and if you don't remain virginal in any way shape or form, whether it's kissing a guy or wearing a certain amount of make up or style of clothing, you're a total slut. Woooow. Zo, just because you're a goddamn prude it doesn't mean everyone else should be, and you shouldn't try to lecture your female readers on their sexuality. Just because you're ashamed of sexuality, it doesn't mean that's a good thing because you happened to be a main character. Also it's pretty obvious you're jealous you yourself can't be that proud. <br /><br />Zoey's friends were all painful stereotypes. Especially her girl friend... what's her name again... I don't know. My mind shut her out because she was too damn annoying. Oh wait... Steve or something. -coughs- anyway, yeah. That chick was an obvious out there comic-relief and completely uncalled for. Every time she said anything I wanted to punch her. I didn't care much for her gay friend either. He was just a cliched gay. And no, I don't have anything against homosexuals. That would be awfully hypocritical since I'm a very out of the closet homosexual myself. But this guy was boring and cliched. <br />Then there's the queen Bee arch rival. -yawn- Oh here's something I haven't seen before... Oh and Zoey falls in love with some vampire guy after he reads a speech from Shakespeare in his sexy vampire hunk voice. So within two seconds, Zoey is in love. True love, yada yada, he's the one, he's so hot, all her friends support her love, bla bla bla, gush gush gush. Then I closed the book. <br /><br />What a piece of overrated, stinky, shitty tripe. The writing was ridiculous, all the characters were boring and annoying and cliched to death, and the overall plot was pulled out of both authors nailed shut asshole. It was ridiculous. The whole book was bloody ridiculous. What on earth was I reading? -shudder- I can't believe this book was published, let alone so well received. And don't give me that 'it's an amazing booooooook and you're just jealooooousssss' crap. Please. It's an awful excuse for a book and I would rather watch 2 girls 1 cup again (from the beginning to the end this time) than have Marked by P.C Crap and Kristin Crap sitting on my shelf. <br /></span>

<div id="review_246991475" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/246991475" />
    <a title="Danielle." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7005742-danielle"><img alt="Danielle." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1506227599p2/7005742.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/246991475?book_show_action=true">Dec 14, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Danielle." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Danielle." href="/user/show/7005742-danielle">Danielle.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7005742-danielle?shelf=annoying-character-s">annoying-character-s</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer246991475" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12601702448214094629">Okay, I'm going to be posting gifs on this review because this book was just too much.<br/>My overall expression after reading up to 150 pages:<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380364934ra/716736.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I wish I could give this 'no star' or something of the sort. I don't even know where to <i>begin</i> with this 'book'. It was retched, horrible, disdainful, etc. etc. P.C. Cast as well as her daughter's writing is childish. All the girls had blonde hair (auburn-blonde, strawberry-blonde, blonde, curly blonde, etc.) it's irritating and the only girl, besides Zoey, tha</span>
  <span id="freeText12601702448214094629" style="display:none">Okay, I'm going to be posting gifs on this review because this book was just too much.<br>My overall expression after reading up to 150 pages:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380364934ra/716736.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I wish I could give this 'no star' or something of the sort. I don't even know where to <i>begin</i> with this 'book'. It was retched, horrible, disdainful, etc. etc. P.C. Cast as well as her daughter's writing is childish. All the girls had blonde hair (auburn-blonde, strawberry-blonde, blonde, curly blonde, etc.) it's irritating and the only girl, besides Zoey, that didn't have blonde hair was Shaunee... and she was black.<br><br>I don't care if this book was completely fiction and that it didn't have to be realistic, but when you write how the reason these celebrities are amazing and known is because they're vamps, I'm going to say you're an idiot. Zoey is the biggest hypocrite and I never liked her, not even for a bit. My friend told me she dated four boys at once. Wasn't she shit talking girls in this book for doing stuff like that, though? I want to scream. <br><br><b>This book had:</b><br>Annoying teen girls.<br>Ridiculous passages.<br>Try-hard humour.<br><br>...Shall I continue? <br><br><b>Offensive and ridiculous passages:</b><br><br>'...One was black, with impossibly long hair (must be a really good weave)...' <br><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380364934ra/716737.gif" width="250" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>These authors see black women with short, crappy hair? And if they do have long, beautiful hair it's automatically a weave? How rude. <br><br>'...the Mark had somehow made my eyes look even bigger and darker. I lined them with a smoky black shadow that had little sparkly flecks of silver in it. Not heavily like those loser girls who think that plastering on black eyeliner makes them look cool. Yeah, <i>right</i>. They look like scary raccoons.'<br><br>Loser girls? LOL, okay. <br><br>'"Is that a bathroom?" I asked as we hurried past water fountains situated between two doors.<br>"Yep," she said. "Here's my class, and there's yours right next door. See you after class!"<br>"Okay, thanks," I called.<br>At least the bathroom was close. If I had a case of raging nervous-stomach diarrhoea I wouldn't have to run far.'<br><br>Really? That very last sentence really was not needed. They could have at least wrote, 'At least the bathroom was close in case of an immense emergency.' or something like that.<br><br>'I've only had detention once so far, and that wasn't my fault. Really. Some turd boy told me to suck his cock. What was I supposed to do? Cry? Giggle? Pout? <i>Umm...no...</i> So instead I bitch-slapped him (although I prefer just using the word smacked)...'<br><br>If you prefer using the word 'smacked' then maybe you should have done? 'Turd boy'? <br><br>'"So, what preconceived notions do you have about Amazon warriors?" she asked the class.<br>A blonde who sat on the other side of the room said, "The Amazons were heavily matriarchal, as are all vampyre societies."<br>Jeesh, she sounded smart.'<br><br>No, she just paid attention in class. <br><br>'I had no idea an hour had passed; the ringing bell was a total surprise. I'd just shoved my sociology book back in my cubbie (okay, I know that Damien and Neferet called them <i>cabinets</i>, but come on -- they totally remind me of the cubbies we used to have in kindergarten)...'<br><br>Oh, God...<br><br>'The door opened an <i>oh my sweet lord</i> I do believe my heart totally stopped beating. I'm positive my mouth flopped open like a moron. He was the most gorgeous young lad I had ever seen.'<br><br>LOL.<br><br>'"yeah, like having poopies for brains," I said, staring down the hall like the slug's back.'<br><br>I don't know what she's trying to prove using the word 'poopie'. Who even says that?<br><br>'Lunch was a huge build-your-own salad buffet, which included everything from tuna salad (eesh) to those weird mini-corns that are so confusing, and don't even taste like corn. (What exactly are they? Baby corn? Midget corn? Mutant corn?'<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380364934ra/716738.gif" width="250" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>'The whole place had that sawdusty, horsey smell that mixed with leather to form something that was pleasant, even though you know that part of the "pleasant" was poopie -- horse poopie.'<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380364934ra/716739.gif" width="250" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Nobody</i> finds the smell of 'horse poopie' pleasant. <b>
  <i>Nobody</i>
</b>.<br><br>'"Zoey! There you are!"<br>"Ohmygod! Stevie Rae! You scared the poo out of me!"'<br><br>Lord, help these so-called 'writers'. Please. <br><br>I dropped the book after that. I'm done. I <b>refuse</b> to finish this book. Everyone thinks Twilight is bad? Twilight doesn't have a damn thing on this crappy excuse of a book. The writing of this 'book' makes Twilight seem as though it was perfectly written (okay, I'm over-exaggerating a tad bit, but it's still better than this. At least I read through the whole book and that's saying something. Am I right, or am I right?) I mean, really, the average user rating for this is 3.83 stars? WOW. Just WOW.<br><br>Let me also add that these authors think they've done an amazing job with sounding like teenagers.... riiiiight... keep telling yourselves that.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12601702448214094629" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16202751911521762312"><b> Full Review </b><br/><br/>Wow, I really hated this book, more specifically, I hated Zoey. I can't believe there are 12 books of her as the MC. This is where I stop with this series<br/><br/>- First of all, Zoey is such a hateful person. I don’t think I have read about an MC that radiates such negative energy in my life. This girl calls every girl she doesn’t like terrible names like bitches, hags, sluts, hos. She thinks she is somehow better than them.   <span id="freeText16202751911521762312" style="display:none"><b> Full Review </b><br /><br />Wow, I really hated this book, more specifically, I hated Zoey. I can't believe there are 12 books of her as the MC. This is where I stop with this series<br /><br />- First of all, Zoey is such a hateful person. I don’t think I have read about an MC that radiates such negative energy in my life. This girl calls every girl she doesn’t like terrible names like bitches, hags, sluts, hos. She thinks she is somehow better than them. Her group of friends are like her and there was no one person amongst them that I actually liked<br /><br />- I know having a special MC is a thing in Ya but this was just ridiculous. The special snowflake syndrome was real in this. It was so annoying how literally everyone she speaks to, reminds her of how special/different she was.<br /><br />- I wanted to read this book because of the vampire storyline but there was hardly any present in this. This book actually removed all the good parts of being a vampire (the transformation, having fangs, just overall, looking scary). Honestly, these people seemed more like witches (with their circles and sayings) and less like vampires<br /><br />- the romance was laughable. Why did erik like her?? I honestly thought he was up to something (maybe he is in later books) because I just couldn't fathom such devotion to someone he didn't really know and wasn't even likeable. <br /><br />Overall, this book was lame, the vampires were pathetic, the characters were hateful, the MC is unlikeable and i hope she dies at the end<br /><br /><b> Pre-reading </b><br />For someone who had a vampire-obsessed stage, I can't believe Twilight was the only vampire book I read. I hope to change that with this lol.</span>

<div id="review_182842456" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/182842456" />
    <a title="Wildbriar" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3961204-wildbriar"><img alt="Wildbriar" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1350850274p2/3961204.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/182842456?book_show_action=true">Jul 07, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wildbriar" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wildbriar" href="/user/show/3961204-wildbriar">Wildbriar</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Absolutely nobody</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3961204-wildbriar?shelf=abandoned">abandoned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3961204-wildbriar?shelf=cover-designer-should-be-shot">cover-designer-should-be-shot</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3961204-wildbriar?shelf=disliked">disliked</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3961204-wildbriar?shelf=wasted-opportunity">wasted-opportunity</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3961204-wildbriar?shelf=waste-of-paper">waste-of-paper</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3961204-wildbriar?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3961204-wildbriar?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3961204-wildbriar?shelf=wary-of-disappointment">wary-of-disappointment</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3961204-wildbriar?shelf=characters-to-be-keelhauled">characters-to-be-keelhauled</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3961204-wildbriar?shelf=shallow">shallow</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer182842456" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15458298029501576241"><br/>To be quite honest, I almost don't know what to say, or how to say it. I read just under half of Marked this morning, then set it gently aside and stared at the wall in a numb silence for a while. Perhaps, in hindsight, I should have thrown it. Marked is, quite simply, the worst book I have ever read in my entire life. Forget one star, this book has achieved negative stars from me.<br/><br/> The horror began with the Acknowledgements. P.C. Cast actually thanked her daughter for making sure they sounded li</span>
  <span id="freeText15458298029501576241" style="display:none"><br />To be quite honest, I almost don't know what to say, or how to say it. I read just under half of Marked this morning, then set it gently aside and stared at the wall in a numb silence for a while. Perhaps, in hindsight, I should have thrown it. Marked is, quite simply, the worst book I have ever read in my entire life. Forget one star, this book has achieved negative stars from me.<br /><br /> The horror began with the Acknowledgements. P.C. Cast actually thanked her daughter for making sure they sounded like teenagers. She actually thanked – for making sure – excuse me please while I go and die in a corner. I didn't exactly laugh, but the further I got into this book, the more horribly ironic that comment became. I have never heard teenagers speak this way, and with such unrelenting consistency. And all the pathetic pop culture name-dropping! Cease. And. Desist. Please! And so the hell never ended, from the Acknowledgements to page 117, where I gave up.<br /><br /> One of the author comments on the back proclaims Marked's hot and funny darkness. Er...only in the way your house goes dark during a powercut; it's intensely irritating, you feel like you can't live like this any longer and you'd do anything to get the electricity back on. You start to go mad, losing your mind as you bump into walls trying to find where you left your last remaining torch with full batteries. It's about as funny as stubbing your toes on the corner of a shelf, several times in a row. That is what it was like reading Marked, painfully navigating my way through it trying to find a plot, character development, tension, excitement, drama, hell <i>anything!</i> The characters, I loathed the characters! Caricatures, the lot of them, and I hated them all, right down to the very last one. I am not going to go into all the tiny details that made me want to kill somebody, but I can at least say that I have finally found a protagonist that I hate more than Nora Grey and Bella Swan. There is nothing in Zoey's head, nothing, except for rotting goo and the odd dead centipede. I could hear my brain cells screaming in protest as they were forced, time and time again, to read each heinous sentence, each word of gut-wrenchingly awful dialogue.<br /><br />Never in a million years did I think I would advocate World Book Burning Day, but if we had one Marked should be the first to go up in smoke; off to Tree Heaven, free at last from being bound in this absolute travesty of a book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15458298029501576241" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3503781353895059569">The easiest rating I've ever given a book. Let us please bury the fact I gave <i>Marked</i> four stars upon first reading; I was only 14 or 15 at the time and in <i>that</i> stage of adolescence-- the fangirling, over-excitable stage which no person wants to look back on. Gah. So embarrassing.<br/><br/>But then, a few days ago, I stumbled upon <i>Marked</i> again in the library. I was curious as to what I'd think of the book now I'd grown up a bit (in both senses of the word). And my brother was still trying to hunt down a bi</span>
  <span id="freeText3503781353895059569" style="display:none">The easiest rating I've ever given a book. Let us please bury the fact I gave <i>Marked</i> four stars upon first reading; I was only 14 or 15 at the time and in <i>that</i> stage of adolescence-- the fangirling, over-excitable stage which no person wants to look back on. Gah. So embarrassing.<br><br>But then, a few days ago, I stumbled upon <i>Marked</i> again in the library. I was curious as to what I'd think of the book now I'd grown up a bit (in both senses of the word). And my brother was still trying to hunt down a big fat textbook for his International Relations classes, so I had plenty of time for a flick-through. <br><br>I grabbed the book and curled up on the library's second-floor window ledge, which overlooks Chamberlain Square. I was even kind of excited, because I had fond memories of staying up all night to devour the pages of this series. <br>But it only took me a few page-skims to come to the (pretty obvious) realisation. The slut-shaming; the name-dropping; the stereotypes; the pre-teen writing; the glorification of the protagonist and demonisation of her rival....what other conclusion could I come to?<br><br><b>Only one.</b><br><br><br>This book....is a GREAT BIG STEAMING PILE OF TURD.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380335966ra/694583.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>That is all.</span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/33615010?book_show_action=true">Sep 23, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katy Johnson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katy Johnson" href="/user/show/81990-katy-johnson">Katy Johnson</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer33615010" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6777491185241189982">This was a really quick read, made even quicker by skipping over the pages of repetitive neo-pagan-vampyre rituals (which I could have done entirely without). The author is clearly trying to win over the wiccan-teen demographic, while appealing to those who loved the Twilight series. <br/><br/>What bugged me most about this one was the author's attempt to address every controversial teen issue imaginable, while instilling good morals without being condescending. She managed, but honestly, the random comme</span>
  <span id="freeText6777491185241189982" style="display:none">This was a really quick read, made even quicker by skipping over the pages of repetitive neo-pagan-vampyre rituals (which I could have done entirely without). The author is clearly trying to win over the wiccan-teen demographic, while appealing to those who loved the Twilight series. <br /><br />What bugged me most about this one was the author's attempt to address every controversial teen issue imaginable, while instilling good morals without being condescending. She managed, but honestly, the random commentary on sex, drugs, alcohol, homosexuality, religious fundamentalism, paganism, etc., felt forced and way too obvious. I'm all about being honest with young adult readers, but you also have to give them some credit and trust they will be able to decipher subtlety. <br /><br />I plan to read the rest of the series, not because the story was terribly alluring, or the characters very interesting, but because I'd like to see if the author evolves as a writer. I'm also interested in seeing whether she decides to scratch her attempts at "relating" to young readers by dropping pop culture references awkwardly throughout the novel (Sarah Jessica Parker, Ashley Simpson, America's Next Top Model, Steve Madden flats....this book is going to be dated in less than three years).</span>
  <a data-text-id="6777491185241189982" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer819013077" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7156243997402877236"><b>EDIT: 28/03/14</b> I finally remember what <i>Marked</i> reminds me of. It reminds me of that horrible Harry Potter fanfiction <a href='https://www.fanfiction.net/s/6829556/1/My-Immortal' rel='nofollow noopener'>My Immortal</a>. They're basically the same, except <i>Marked</i> has much better spelling. (Thankfully).<br/><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1394895612i/8921420.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Well, hell. I finished <i>Marked</i>.<br/><br/><i>Marked</i> is not the worst book I have ever read. <i>Halo</i> still tops that list. But, damn, I haven't rolled my eyes so much since...since anything, actually. I actually took the liberty to tab every single annoying line in <i>Marked</i>, and here is how many post-its I was</span>
  <span id="freeText7156243997402877236" style="display:none"><b>EDIT: 28/03/14</b> I finally remember what <i>Marked</i> reminds me of. It reminds me of that horrible Harry Potter fanfiction <a href="https://www.fanfiction.net/s/6829556/1/My-Immortal" rel="nofollow noopener">My Immortal</a>. They're basically the same, except <i>Marked</i> has much better spelling. (Thankfully).<br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1394895612i/8921420.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Well, hell. I finished <i>Marked</i>.<br><br><i>Marked</i> is not the worst book I have ever read. <i>Halo</i> still tops that list. But, damn, I haven't rolled my eyes so much since...since anything, actually. I actually took the liberty to tab every single annoying line in <i>Marked</i>, and here is how many post-its I wasted:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1394895612i/8921421._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>My post-its are separated into a few main categories:<br>-World building<br>-Idiot<br>-Special snowflake/Mary Sue<br>-Judging<br>-Stereotyping<br>-Name dropping<br><br>I will address each of them individually, but first:<br><br><u>The plot</u><br><b>Join <s>idiot</s> Zoey Redbird, as she embarks on a <s>boring</s> heroic quest to kick a slutty ho out of the student council.</b><br><br>After Zoey Redbird was mysteriously marked, she goes to a fucking boarding school for vampyres. She meets a slutty ho, Aphrodite, and decides she hates her. She, her cardboard-cutout friends, and her insta-love for Erik will work together to defeat Aphrodite by deus ex machina, and praying. <br><br>This is what the whole fucking book is about. It's fine if there's not much of a plot of it's meant to be character-driven. Sadly, I can tell that <i>Marked</i> was supposed to be more plot-driven.<br><br><u>World building</u><br>I don't see many other reviewers addressing this problem, but the world building <i>fucking drove me crazy</i>. <br><br>From the blurb: <i>The House of Night series is set in a world very much like our own, except in 16-year-old Zoey Redbird's world, vampyres have always existed.</i><br><br>Sure, why the fuck not? But <i>Marked</i> does such a fucking crappy job on executing it. Fuck, it's even labelled as a fucking fantasy! Why would people know so little about vampires if they existed for so long? Why <i>the fuck</i> would there be only one vampire boarding school? If vampires existed for so long, wouldn't they have gone to war with humans? They're so much more powerful than them, after all. Why the hell would people discriminate against vampires if "vampyres were attractive and the most successful actors and actresses in the world"?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380408367ra/798844.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><u>
  <b>Zoey Redbird</b>
</u><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1381909553ra/5406828.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>She's...I don't... Fuck, I don't know how to start. Zoey Redbird is a fucking idiot. She has the most idiotic thoughts ever.<br><br><i>If I died, would it get me out of my geometry test tomorrow? One could only hope.</i><br><br><i>Wow! Who knew hitting my head and passing out would be so much fun?</i><br><br><i>Hee hee, Mom was mad at her, too.</i><br><br><i>Speaking of boobs—I was totally sounding like one. (boob...hee hee).</i><br><br><i>Hee hee...vamp vets...I could call my clinic Vamp Vets, and the ads would read:"We'll take your blood for free!"</i><br><br><i>I'd just shoved my sociology book back into my cubbie (okay, I know that Damien and Neferet called them cabinets, but come on—they totally remind me of the cubbies we used to have in kindergarten)</i><br><br><i>"Yeah, like having poopie for brains."</i><br><br><i>Mini-corns are so confusing, and don't even taste like corn. (What exactly are that? Baby corn? Midget corn? Mutant corn?)</i><br><br><i>"Ohmygod! Stevie Rae! You scared the poo out of me!"</i><br><br><i>I wished it was cold and Kayla would freeze her over-developed boobies right off.</i><br><br><i>Maybe she'd taken a shower this morning and melted when the water touched her—hee hee.</i><br><br><i>me gusta Erik</i><br><br><i>Aphrodite laughed a throaty, I'm-so-grown-up-and-you're-just-a-kid laugh. I really hate it when girls do that. I mean, yes, she's older, but I have boobs, too.</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1394895612ra/8921422.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>She thinks about the most obvious things.<br><br><i>Lit class was an experience.</i><br>Yeah... Everything you experience is an experience.<br><br><i>The hour definitely seemed to take an hour</i><br>No shit, Sherlock.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1394895612i/8921423._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>P.C. Cast and Kristen Cast congratulate each other for sounding like teenagers. I have no fucking idea why they do. Kristen Cast was in college when she co-wrote this, for fuck's sake! Did she not experience being a teenager? Because I can assure you, <i>no teenager speaks like that</i>.<br><br><u>Mary Sue</u><br>Zoey Redbird is definitely the most annoying protagonist ever. Apart from her stupid thoughts, she is also a Mary Sue, and a fucking Spesul Snowflake.<br><br>Did you know Zoey can control all the five elements? Zoey can control the five elements. She's very special. She's got a colored-in mark. She doesn't think she's special, but oh, she is! She got touched by the goddess, Nyx! (no, Nyx didn't touch her there). Nyx likes Zoey very much. Yes, Zoey is very special. Zoey can control all the five elements. She's pretty, did you know that? She's very beautiful. She caught the eye of Erik, the hottest guy in school. Also, she has the affinity for all five elements. It has never happened before, not even in High Priestesses! She's very, very special. Animals also like her. She's very special.<br><br>That is how the entire fucking 306 pages went.<br>The <s>idiots</s> Casts never skip an opportunity to remind us how fucking special Zoey is. She can control the elements. Big fucking deal.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1394895612ra/8921424.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><u>Judging you</u><br>Zoey judges every <i>fucking</i> person she meets. She calls people "ho"s, "loser"s or "slug"s.<br>She calls her brother troll-like, and her sister a slut. She calls religious women fat, and religious men pedophiles. She calls anorexic girls freak-like. Anyone who is called "Aphrodite" is automatically slutty. Unattractive people are losers.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1394895612ra/8921425.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Wanna hear my theory about how my generation could single-handedly wipe out slugs and loser kids from America?</i><br>This fucking quote. I can't even.<br>This is why so many kids commit suicide. They are judged by people like Zoey. They could be clever, they could have talent, and yet you just label them as "loser". Just fucking no.<br><br>You're neither a slut nor a loser, you say? Well, pick one because in Zoey's eyes, you are either one of them.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1394895612ra/8921426.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>In Zoey's eyes, everyone else is an idiot, whereas she is perfect.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1394895612ra/8921427.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><u>Stereotyping</u><br><i>Marked</i> doesn't streotype as much as <i>Halo</i>, but it still had a large amount of stereotyping to it. Here's the Zoey Redbird stereotyping quiz!<br>1)Do you have big boobies? (Hee hee, boobies!)<br>If yes, then you are a slut!<br><br>2)Do you have a high-pitched giggle?<br>If yes, then you are a ho!<br><br>3)Do you like wearing black and putting on eyeliner?<br>If yes, then you are a Goth!<br><br>4)Do you wear baggy pants?<br>If yes, then you are a gang-wannabe!<br><br>5)Have you had sex before?<br>If yes, then you are one of those girls who has sex with everyone and think that they're not going to get pregnant or a really nasty STD that eats your brains and stuff! (Don't believe me? We'll see in ten years!)<br><br>6)Are you thin?<br>If yes, then you are a freak girl who pukes and starves themselves into what they think is Paris Hilton chic!<br><br>7)Have you had oral sex before?<br>If yes, then you don't have a functioning brain!<br><br>8)Are you a rich kid?<br>If yes, then you must be doing drugs!<br><br>9)Have you ever made out with a girl in public? (Only applicable for girls)<br>If yes, then you are a moron!<br><br>10)Do you put on a lot of black eyeliner? (Only applicable for girls)<br>If yes, then you are a loser girl who looks like a scary raccoon!<br><br>11)Are you blond?<br>If yes, then you can't possibly be smart!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1394895612ra/8921428.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><u>Name Dropping</u><br>What is with all the name dropping in <i>Marked</i>? There's Madonna, there's Paris Hilton, there's Leonardo Dicaprio, and so many other ones I am too lazy to type.<br><br>I know brands are a huge part of our lives, but why do the Casts feel the need to name drop every fucking page? <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1394895612ra/8921429.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><u>The romance</u><br>Bullshit. Zoey and Erik's relationship was 100% insta-love. What's worse is that their eyes first locked over Aphrodite sucking Erik's cock. I'm serious. Aphrodite is forcing a blow-job on Erik, and Zoey sees them. Their fucking eyes lock together. They fucking fall in love. <br>Excuse me, but what? <br>And suddenly Erik is falling head over heels for Zoey. Sorry, but their romance is too unbelievable. More like Erik was there so Zoey would seem more desirable.<br><br><u>Zoey's cardboard cut-out friends</u><br>Zoey's friends serve no other purpose than to make Zoey seem more lovable and special. Really, they can't stop gushing over how pretty/great Zoey is. Daimen is the typical best gay, Shaunee and Erin, I don't even know what purpose they serve, and Stevie Rae is the typical best friend. <br><br>The conclusion is, unless you want a headache, stay away from <i>Marked</i>.<br><br>Seriously, if you are reading it out of curiosity, I can tell you that it is as bad as you think. Walk away, and be happy that you never had to read this.<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="7156243997402877236" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_379367948" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/379367948" />
    <a title="Anushka" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8377084-anushka"><img alt="Anushka" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1452007230p2/8377084.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/379367948?book_show_action=true">Jul 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anushka" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anushka" href="/user/show/8377084-anushka">Anushka</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8377084-anushka?shelf=everyone-loved-it-but-me">everyone-loved-it-but-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8377084-anushka?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8377084-anushka?shelf=major-facepalm">major-facepalm</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8377084-anushka?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8377084-anushka?shelf=disappointed">disappointed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8377084-anushka?shelf=overrated">overrated</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer379367948" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3775106232307484475"><b>{1.5 Stars}</b><br/><br/>Okaaaay. So my theory is this - Overly hyped books like <i>House of Night</i> and <i>Mortal Instruments</i> were released near 2005 when there were very few YA Fantasy books and that's the reason these books are so famous. I mean, people are totally crazy about HoN & MI even though there are many books which are much better than these. <br/>So, <i>House of Night</i>.<br/>This book had a <b>weak plot</b>, weak as in <u> pointless plot</u>.<br/><br/><i>Why did Zoey get 'Marked'? And why especially by the Goddess Nyx?</i> <br/>The author didn't have any</span>
  <span id="freeText3775106232307484475" style="display:none"><b>{1.5 Stars}</b><br /><br />Okaaaay. So my theory is this - Overly hyped books like <i>House of Night</i> and <i>Mortal Instruments</i> were released near 2005 when there were very few YA Fantasy books and that's the reason these books are so famous. I mean, people are totally crazy about HoN &amp; MI even though there are many books which are much better than these. <br />So, <i>House of Night</i>.<br />This book had a <b>weak plot</b>, weak as in <u> pointless plot</u>.<br /><br /><i>Why did Zoey get 'Marked'? And why especially by the Goddess Nyx?</i> <br />The author didn't have any theory; she just had to make her character special so there! Nyx herself does it. <br /><br />Getting 'Marked' means getting a half crescent moon shaped on forehead which signifies that the human will go through some changes to become an adult Vampire. And to learn to become a Vampire, the ‘fledgling’ is sent to a school called House of Night. As told in the story several times, not all fledglings survive this some of them die at a very early stage or some die when they are almost about to. But obviously our lead survives it because she was given the mark by Nyx for not-even-author-knows-what reason.<br /><br /><b>The writing</b> - its <u>irritating</u>! That is the only word that comes to mind.<br />Zoey and her friends bicker like fifth graders! P.C. Cast had done this on purpose so that it'd feel like we're reading book by a teenager (She mentioned this in acknowledgements, I'm not making it up) but I'm really sorry to say Cast-ladies that readers feel like they are reading diary entry of a bunch of bimbos instead! <br />They are so darn corny and unfunny you'd want to drag them through their hair. With every page I read I felt a bit more dumber and dumber. Their group just keeps chittering and chattering to no extent. Anything they say has no use in the story; it is just included to increase the thickness of the book. When this was not enough, there's the gang of Dark Daughters who try to imitate Plastics from <i>Mean Girls</i>. Their group leader's name is Aphrodite, APHRODITE for God's sake!! Who has names like that anymore? And how can you go around flaunting and being a bitch to everyone with such a name? I would die of shame.<br /><br />The authors have tried to create the environment of a high school in Vampire format, <i>tried to</i>. You can just tell by the language that they've tried way too hard to do that. All the girls keep squeaking all the time and talk about hot guys as if they have nothing else to do. <br /><br />The book covers the events of 2 or 3 days but in that short span of time itself Zoey finds a soul-mate. (Boy, I wish it was that easy for me too.) Erik is supposedly a out-of-the-world hot guy who winks at Zoey in a classroom full of people the first time he sees her and the next time he meets her, they kiss. And the third time they meet he tells her "that you make me feel different". <b>HOW STUPID IS THAT?!</b> They don't even exchanged names properly but start sloshing their tongues down each other throats because they are apparently 'made for each other'. <br /><br />Everything about <i>Marked</i> screamed <b>stupid, immature, senseless, waste-of-time literature</b> to me! Ugh! To sum it up in one line - I simply <b>hated</b> it!<br /><br />But...I gave the book 1.5 stars because by excluding the useless chitter-chatter between the characters and replacing them with some sensible adult conversations this would've been more bearable (maybe).<br />I wouldn't recommend this book to anyone, but I am going to read the 2nd book sometime later only because a friend of mine (although, I have huge doubts about it now) is a huge fan of the series and she is forcing me to. <br />Lord, save my soul! D:</span>
  <a data-text-id="3775106232307484475" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_8134993" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/8134993" />
    <a title="Shannon (Giraffe Days)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/395599-shannon-giraffe-days"><img alt="Shannon (Giraffe Days)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1420332941p2/395599.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/8134993?book_show_action=true">Oct 23, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shannon (Giraffe Days)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shannon (Giraffe Days)" href="/user/show/395599-shannon-giraffe-days">Shannon (Giraffe Days)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/395599-shannon-giraffe-days?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/395599-shannon-giraffe-days?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/395599-shannon-giraffe-days?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/395599-shannon-giraffe-days?shelf=2007">2007</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/395599-shannon-giraffe-days?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer8134993" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16385563553981933574">16 year old Zoey has a crappy home life, an almost-ex-boyfriend who drinks too much, a best friend who's shallow and a geometry test tomorrow. But all this matters for naught when she is Marked by a Vampyre Tracker and must move to the House of Night school in Tulsa, Oklahoma, for four years while her body undergoes the Change into a Vampyre - or rejects it and she dies.<br/><br/>This is a new and original take on the Vampire legends, and mixes in matriarchy and goddess-worship with pleasing effect. Zoey </span>
  <span id="freeText16385563553981933574" style="display:none">16 year old Zoey has a crappy home life, an almost-ex-boyfriend who drinks too much, a best friend who's shallow and a geometry test tomorrow. But all this matters for naught when she is Marked by a Vampyre Tracker and must move to the House of Night school in Tulsa, Oklahoma, for four years while her body undergoes the Change into a Vampyre - or rejects it and she dies.<br /><br />This is a new and original take on the Vampire legends, and mixes in matriarchy and goddess-worship with pleasing effect. Zoey becomes marked in a special way - the Goddess Nyx has given her a special responsibility and added gifts; which she'll need, because something's not right at the House of Night, and her own mentor and High Priestess may not be the gentle, caring mother-figure she makes herself out to be.<br /><br />What I especially liked about this book was how it handles issues relevant to teenagers. Yes it discusses topics like drinking, drugs, anorexia, sex, homosexuality, bullying etc. but all in a positive light (or an "anti-" light, depending on the topic). Zoey is a wonderful role model with a sensible head on her shoulders who looks beyond the surface to what really makes people behave how they do. <br /><br />Also, to be perfectly clear on this point, despite what you might have read, there is no sex in this book, or the sequel (and even if there was, I think it would be handled very maturely). There is some slutty behaviour from one of the characters, but this is hardly glorified. In fact, it's only the language of the teenaged characters themselves that stops this book from being too moralising. The slang etc. has been captured perfectly, but is not overdone so that it gets really annoying. It's also dark, funny, and the inclusion of rituals invoking the five elements of air, water, fire, earth and spirit add a new, beautiful element that I really liked. I honestly think this book and the ones that follow can only have a good impression on teenagers. Don't be afraid to put it on your library's shelves. In fact, my biggest problem with this book was the rather excessive product placement going on. It's unnecessary and grotesque. Otherwise, <i>Marked</i> is highly enjoyable!</span>
  <a data-text-id="16385563553981933574" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_168827800" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/168827800" />
    <a title="Annie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5038179-annie"><img alt="Annie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600930180p2/5038179.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/168827800?book_show_action=true">May 16, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Annie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Annie" href="/user/show/5038179-annie">Annie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">The slum of society </span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5038179-annie?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5038179-annie?shelf=crap">crap</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5038179-annie?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5038179-annie?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer168827800" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17024643362292863544">This is – literally – the worst (published) book I have ever read in my life. Every time I so much as think about this book, or this series in general, I suddenly have the urge to take a nine iron to an old lady, or set a kitten on fire or something else just as random and pointless that won’t actually solve my hatred towards this piece of crap but will help release some of my anger because Zoey is only a fictional character and I can’t actually kill her will a dull axe. *deep breath* It’s times</span>
  <span id="freeText17024643362292863544" style="display:none">This is – literally – the worst (published) book I have ever read in my life. Every time I so much as think about this book, or this series in general, I suddenly have the urge to take a nine iron to an old lady, or set a kitten on fire or something else just as random and pointless that won’t actually solve my hatred towards this piece of crap but will help release some of my anger because Zoey is only a fictional character and I can’t actually kill her will a dull axe. *deep breath* It’s times like these where unpublished authors know they stand a chance: if shit like this cannot only be published but actually become incredibly popular, you know you could write a bestseller in a COMA. <br /><br />There’s no need to mention the writing is atrocious; anybody who picks it up will tell you that. Every single character has a voice that’s like nails on a chalkboard. You know Janice, from “Friends”? Yeah, that’s the voice I give to Zoey. Totally fits, doesn’t it? Everything about this book screams juvenile, and I’m not talking about that preteen way which is fine, if this book is written for that age group, it’s just plain stupid. Sixteen year olds should be insulted by how they’re portrayed in this, and if they aren’t, and actually relate to these “characters”, they need to be terminated immediately. Everything about this is one big stereotype, from the gay people to the black people to the Southern girl, and funnily enough, Zoey thinks she’s better than all of them, and she’s too stupid to live. She thinks a normally constructed sentence is “amazing vocab”. <br /><br />Every chapter, every paragraph, every sentence annoyed me. The showing, not telling. The unrealistic dialogue. Zoey. The fucking Twins. The shallow relationships (Zoey has best friends and a guy saying how he cares about her “from his heart” in ONE NIGHT?). Zoey. The religion. The vampires that are not vampires, but witches. Zoey. The “messages”. Everything. Zoey. Honestly, you’d think with two people writing this, there’s two brains involved, which should mean that at some point, there should have been at least ONE good example of writing: a piece of dialogue, some description, some semi-decent prose that didn’t have me wanting to kill the friend who leant this to me. <br /><br />And can I just mention how much of a Harry Potter rip off this is? You’ve got the “protagonist” (haha) with a mark on her forehead, making her the Chosen One, and is sent off to some fancy boarding school for magical people like her. Because of this special mark, everyone knows instantly who she is, having a polarizing effect – some love her, others hate her. Then you’ve got the platinum blonde who’s rich and whines to her dad about how she’s not loved enough who becomes the “protagonist’s” archrival on the first day of school for no reason, other than jealousy of this newfound popularity someone else has. You’ve got the goofy, quirky sidekicks. You’ve got the “protagonist” suddenly being the favourite of the Headmistress and form a special relationship. There are all kinds of cool classes with the odd teachers. Please, this isn’t a Twilight rip off – just because it has vampires doesn’t make it a Twilight rip off. This is so Harry Potter I can’t believe nobody has mentioned it, except Harry Potter is – y’know – amazing. Stephenie Meyer is not as to J.K. Rowling as the Casts are not to Stephenie Meyer. Stephenie Meyer is Shakespeare, the Bronte sisters, Dickens, Tolstoy and anyone else you can think of compared to this garbage. <br /><br />For a long time I judged people’s intelligence on a yard stick, the yard stick being whether or not you liked this book. Then I embarrassingly found out two of my very nice, smart friends actually like this, so huh, who knew. I’m still unwavering though – this is the worst, stupidest book ever written. I’m actually kind of embarrassed to have it on my bookshelf, because people will actually know I’ve read it. Just for the record, it was given to me, and I didn’t want to hurt my friend’s feelings. Not my fault I stumbled on this. In fact, she gave several more to me, and I actually stopped mid-book. I just couldn’t take it anymore.<br /><br />Stupid book. Stupid. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17024643362292863544" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer318850845791924407">**For more reviews, contests, interviews, book news and more go to my blog:<br/><br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://theheelshaveeyes.wordpress.com/'>http://theheelshaveeyes.wordpress.com/</a><br/><br/>Shambles, an absolute bloody shambles is how I can best describe this book.I don’t know what was worse, the tacky and unsympathetic attitude towards eating disorder victims, the blasé attitude towards male rape (the hallway scene, imagine the gender roles reversed and you’ll see how sexist it is) , or the constant usage of the words slut and hoe, oh yeah what a great example we’re set</span>
  <span id="freeText318850845791924407" style="display:none">**For more reviews, contests, interviews, book news and more go to my blog:<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://theheelshaveeyes.wordpress.com/">http://theheelshaveeyes.wordpress.com/</a><br /><br />Shambles, an absolute bloody shambles is how I can best describe this book.I don’t know what was worse, the tacky and unsympathetic attitude towards eating disorder victims, the blasé attitude towards male rape (the hallway scene, imagine the gender roles reversed and you’ll see how sexist it is) , or the constant usage of the words slut and hoe, oh yeah what a great example we’re setting for young girls. Call each other degrading terms because women are apparently so empowered now it doesn't matter. This book is just vile, and worse still it's aimed at teens.These so called writers should be ashamed of themselves, even worse it’s going to be turned into a movie and possibly shoved in our faces for a decade. This is of course, the first book in a series of about 10 or 11, I’m not even sure it’s even finished.<br /><br /> I can see why people are going to get sucked into this, as I almost was, but do yourself a favour, fully analyse the sick values in this book and you will begin to see where I am coming from….as well as hate yourself for at some point having liked it. <br /><br />I think the success of this series comes down to crafty marketing, nice covers and the brain-dead masses. <br /><br /> This book is a weapon of mass destruction to anyone who dare reads it, if you hated Bella Swan, you’re going to want to throw the main protagonist Zoey Redbird on a train track. The clichés in this book made me roll my eyes every two seconds;the dumb blonde and her two ugly sisters, the quiet geeky girl who puts up with the crap from the dumb blonde. I could go on, but I can’t be bothered. <br /><br />Do not read this book, unless you genuinely want to waste 306 pages of reading time.I was going to stop giving bad reviews to books I don’t like because I hate the idea of putting books down, but future victims of bad reviews, can have this book to thank.<br /><br />Oh and one more thing, there is one line that truly, truly PISSED ME OFF!!<br /><br />'Two girls were standing behind her, dressed in much the same way. One was black, with impossibly long hair (must be a really good weave).'<br /><br />WTF, how terribly offensive, plenty of black women grow their hair out naturally and very long. Not all of them wear weaves or even want to, so to suggest that long straight hair is somehow more superior and beautiful than curly afro hair is just rude.<br /><br />Best selling authors, HA! This whole series is a joke, whoever thought it was a good idea to turn it into a movie should have the blood sucked out of them.<br /></span>

<div id="review_96038710" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/96038710" />
    <a title="Thomas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2018505-thomas"><img alt="Thomas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567953607p2/2018505.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/96038710?book_show_action=true">Mar 27, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Thomas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Thomas" href="/user/show/2018505-thomas">Thomas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">No one</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer96038710" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14327323400559903377"><i>Marked</i> is one of the worst written books I've read in a long, long time. It is incomprehensible how an intelligent and/or civilized person could enjoy a book like this. Although it's understandable how someone could get swept up in the average, mundanely composed storyline, the writing - oh man, I think I might have lost a few brain cells. Hopefully reading this book hasn't permanently damaged my own writing.<br/><br/>One of the most annoying things was Zoey, the main character, had a tendency to think in</span>
  <span id="freeText14327323400559903377" style="display:none"><i>Marked</i> is one of the worst written books I've read in a long, long time. It is incomprehensible how an intelligent and/or civilized person could enjoy a book like this. Although it's understandable how someone could get swept up in the average, mundanely composed storyline, the writing - oh man, I think I might have lost a few brain cells. Hopefully reading this book hasn't permanently damaged my own writing.<br /><br />One of the most annoying things was Zoey, the main character, had a tendency to think in random tangents (hee hee, see that alliteration! They all start with t!) She also had a massive, gargantuan amount of immature catchphrases. By the end of the book I felt like ripping my hair out every time I read one of the following: "Oh, hell!" "Oh, crap!" "Ah, crap." "*insert unnecessary cuss word!* Seriously, Cast pretty much included a cuss word or reference to sex or drugs in every other sentence. It's realistic when an author includes the occasional cuss word or discreetly mentioned sexual innuendo. But when the main character starts spewing stupid things like how large her teacher's chest is, it's just plain irritating.<br /><br />Oh, and Zoey has officially earned her rank in the top five most annoying protagonists of all time. I refuse to believe that ANY teenage girl could empathize with her - when people say things like "oh, this book would be perfect for teenage girls!", or "I didn't like this, but a girl might!" I almost cringe in disgust. Zoey is mindless, exasperating, and completely one dimensional. She is pretty much the anti-role model. One moment she's discussing the utter normality of sex, the next moment she's talking about how wrong it is to want to kiss a boy. Hypocrite, anyone?<br /><br />1.5 stars, rounded up to two. The first reason is because after reading this novel I'm more aware of what <i>not</i> to do if I decide to write a book. The second reason is because sometimes the plot was so pointless it was actually funny. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14327323400559903377" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review96038710">

<span id="freeTextContainer5690206801921345798"><i>"Zoey Montgomery! Night has chosen thee; thy death will be thy birth. Night calls to thee; hearken to Her sweet voice. Your destiny awaits you at the House of Night!”</i><br/><br/>Well, several years have passed since the first time I read this series. I remember that it was very entertaining and so unbelievably addictive. I wanted to read one book after the other nonstop. <br/>And I did. <br/><br/>I read the first books in greek translation and the rest in their original version because they hadn't been translated.
