  <span id="freeText5690206801921345798" style="display:none"><i>"Zoey Montgomery! Night has chosen thee; thy death will be thy birth. Night calls to thee; hearken to Her sweet voice. Your destiny awaits you at the House of Night!”</i><br /><br />Well, several years have passed since the first time I read this series. I remember that it was very entertaining and so unbelievably addictive. I wanted to read one book after the other nonstop. <br />And I did. <br /><br />I read the first books in greek translation and the rest in their original version because they hadn't been translated. I don't know if they are translated now in greek language. And I don't care because I have decided to do a reread and read the first books in english as well. I am happy to say that the first book is still as entertaining as I remembered it.<br /><br />The series follows the adventures of Zoey Redbird, a 16 years old girl who has Cherokee heritage. One day she will be chosen to become a new vampire and she will need to attend a school for vampires. Vampires are not dark creatures of the night that humans ignore their existence. Everybody knows that they live among humans and every teenager knows that there is a possibility that he/she may be chosen to join them.<br /><br />I don't remember many details from the series, hence the reread (because I want to write reviews for the books)<br />But I remember four things very clearly:<br /><br />**SPOILERS**<br />1. Zoey gains a new tattoo/mark at the end of almost every book. At least in the first books.<br />2. Vampire girls behave more like witches than vampires with their rituals and their affinity in elements.<br />3. Most of the evil characters, villains and monsters will become well- intentioned misunderstood characters ( with tragic personal stories) at some point and everyone will like them.<br />4. Zoey will be betrayed and heartbroken by her first lover.<br /><br />The first book describes thd first days of Zoey at the House of Night, her new friends, her new enemies and her new wannabe boyfriend.</span>

<div id="review_27675148" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/27675148" />
    <a title="Britt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/72305-britt"><img alt="Britt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1205330902p2/72305.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/27675148?book_show_action=true">Jul 18, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Britt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Britt" href="/user/show/72305-britt">Britt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/72305-britt?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/72305-britt?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/72305-britt?shelf=identity">identity</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/72305-britt?shelf=fantasy-sci-fi">fantasy-sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer27675148" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4870714413857763423">Typical teen story in which there is a black and white delineation between the heroes and the villains, and you will never mistake one for the other. Our heroine comes from a troubled family, longs for a place to belong, is marked as incredibly and shockingly extraordinary amongst her new peers, butts heads with the queen of the school who is also the flatly drawn villainess, immediately catches the eye of the hottest guy at school who is also the ex of our villainess, shows remarkable powers an</span>
  <span id="freeText4870714413857763423" style="display:none">Typical teen story in which there is a black and white delineation between the heroes and the villains, and you will never mistake one for the other. Our heroine comes from a troubled family, longs for a place to belong, is marked as incredibly and shockingly extraordinary amongst her new peers, butts heads with the queen of the school who is also the flatly drawn villainess, immediately catches the eye of the hottest guy at school who is also the ex of our villainess, shows remarkable powers and wields them with a confidence and skill even the most advanced prodigy would not have after one day in a new world with new rules (after suffering from slight self-esteem issues easily erased by her upbeat and encouraging friends), and is wise beyond her years leading her to take on the benevolent savior leader role amongst her friends and eventually the entire school.<br /><br />The author captures the teenage voice well enough (though it did seem she was trying a bit hard at times), but all the pop culture references got annoying. Also, while she did sound like a teenager, the narrator’s voice irritated me. She spent a good deal of time passing harsh judgments against particular types of people and behavior. Girls who wear lots of makeup are losers (as are a great many other people throughout the book). Teenagers drinking and smoking is horrifying and disgusting. Wanting to kiss someone you are attracted to apparently makes you a slut. She dislikes one of her classmates because he is not only annoying but also unattractive. While I am not saying that teenagers having sex and drinking and smoking is a good thing, I felt this moralizing had more to do with the author wanting the kiddies to know how dirty these things are than with the character really holding these opinions. It felt that her reaction to them was more immature than the character the author wanted us to see.<br /><br />Also, not a fan of all the hatred for religion. More of the author pushing her point of view than creating anything compelling within the story. What does this really add? Nothing that couldn’t have been done some other way.<br /><br />The author does more telling than she should, which always annoys me. You don’t need to tell me that you hate homophobes; I can tell that by the way you’re speaking about their intolerance. You don’t need to tell me you’re a dork; I can tell that by the Star Trek sweatshirt you wear. You definitely don’t need to tell me that you have no choice in being the villainess because that is the role you are meant to play, I can tell that by reading the rest of the book. Also not cool? Defining words within the text. Not necessary! Are we writing an SAT prep novel? No!<br /><br />I am getting a bit tired of the vampires who are so much more powerful, beautiful, intelligent, wonderful than humans and have all these amazing abilities and gifts. This just makes it too easy to use these abilities to get out of whatever trouble pops up in the story. Neferet showing up at the Samhain ritual? Why would she? Because she’s intuitive? I’m not buying it. It’s just too convenient.<br /><br />Ok, so, those are some pretty negative bits that I did not like about the book, but I did enjoy it overall. I do like the vampires the author created. I like that becoming a vampire is a biological change that your body could reject, thus killing you. I like that they are mortal and just have a longer life span than humans. I like that they can go out during the day, it’s just really uncomfortable. I like that they have a vampire school. I like that they are part of society, excelling in the arts. I like that vampires have a matriarchal society. I think the mixture of the goddess and vampirism is interesting. I like the main character’s new friends. The concept is interesting and fun, and I will probably pick up the sequels at work tomorrow.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4870714413857763423" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_432284795" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/432284795" />
    <a title="Elise ✘ a.k.a Ryder&#39;s Pet ✘" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13567836-elise-a-k-a-ryder-s-pet"><img alt="Elise ✘ a.k.a Ryder&#39;s Pet ✘" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1387046887p2/13567836.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/432284795?book_show_action=true">Oct 11, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elise ✘ a.k.a Ryder&#39;s Pet ✘" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elise ✘ a.k.a Ryder&#39;s Pet ✘" href="/user/show/13567836-elise-a-k-a-ryder-s-pet">Elise ✘ a.k.a Ryder&#39;s Pet ✘</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6567023-marked">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13567836-elise-a-k-a-ryder-s-pet?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13567836-elise-a-k-a-ryder-s-pet?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13567836-elise-a-k-a-ryder-s-pet?shelf=author-p-c-cast">author-p-c-cast</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13567836-elise-a-k-a-ryder-s-pet?shelf=first-in-series">first-in-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13567836-elise-a-k-a-ryder-s-pet?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13567836-elise-a-k-a-ryder-s-pet?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13567836-elise-a-k-a-ryder-s-pet?shelf=paranomal-general">paranomal-general</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13567836-elise-a-k-a-ryder-s-pet?shelf=3-stars">3-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13567836-elise-a-k-a-ryder-s-pet?shelf=pn-romance">pn-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13567836-elise-a-k-a-ryder-s-pet?shelf=read-more-than-once">read-more-than-once</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer432284795" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15111402755706148324"><blockquote>
  <b>⋰⋱⋰⋱⋰⋱*Too YA For Me*⋰⋱⋰⋱⋰⋱</b>
</blockquote><br/><b>
  <u>Second re-read: 23.03.2020</u>
</b><br/>I've gone back and forth whenever to re-read this book, not just to finally finish the series, but because I remember I truly loved it. I mean, this book/series is kinda important to me as it was the book that made me get into books in the first place. Sure, I've read Twilight Saga before this one, however that just because of Edward Cullen who I fell madly in love with and I needed to know what happened after I watched the movie. But </span>
  <span id="freeText15111402755706148324" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>⋰⋱⋰⋱⋰⋱*Too YA For Me*⋰⋱⋰⋱⋰⋱</b>
</blockquote><br><b>
  <u>Second re-read: 23.03.2020</u>
</b><br>I've gone back and forth whenever to re-read this book, not just to finally finish the series, but because I remember I truly loved it. I mean, this book/series is kinda important to me as it was the book that made me get into books in the first place. Sure, I've read Twilight Saga before this one, however that just because of Edward Cullen who I fell madly in love with and I needed to know what happened after I watched the movie. But Twilight Saga didn't make me want to continue reading books. But Marked did. It so did. I read through this one, and immediately started the sequel and then the next, and the next, and then it was done for.<br><br>As for the dates I've put on on the first two readings is a guess. I seriously don't remember when I read it. That being said... the reason I was quite undecided about reading it or not is because YA doesn't do it for me anymore. I've tried re-reading other YA books that I <i>used</i> to love but ended up disliking them in the re-read. So it's safe to say I was... scared to start this re-read. <br><br>Overall, this re-read wasn't bad. I'm glad I did it and I can totally understand why I used to love it back in the day. I mean, I can imagine how good this book - for me now - could've been <i>if</i> it had been NA. It would've been more mature so that the immatureness wouldn't have bothered me because, if it had been written right - the NA - then there won't have been any immatureness. That said, there was quite some immature scenes, moments and characters... Zoey had her moments of showing her full immature 16 years: like the way she's acting/feeling towards poor Elliott. It would've been easier in this re-read had she been quite a mature 16 year old, but you can't have everything. But yeah, I do understand why I loved it before. I was around the same age back then and could probably (I don't remember) relate to Zoey more? And there's <s>hot</s> cute guys, action, mystery and friendship... It just lacks maturity.<br><br>Though there is only one certain character that truly made my heart beat and that I'm actually excited to meet again, and who I won't meet for a few books. Guess in the comments who it is... That being said, the timeline is a bit... short on things. Like, they are speaking about feeling things with their hearts after two days... insta-love is not for me, as you all know. Luckily I know what's gonna happen so I can look away from certain things, but still, it kinda bothers me with everything happening in the span of a couple of days - three days to be exact, which is way too short - for me at least - to bond truly. So while the book has potential for the me <i>now</i>, it's still you know, YA and immature and all that, but understandable as to why I used to love it. Now it's just meh for me. I've taken the book from my ‘favorites’ shelf as it's no longer a favorite. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1584991997i/29154607.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b><u>The Characters</u>:</b> <i>(some information is taken for House of Night Wiki)</i><br><i>The list is long so I've put it in a spoilers tag.</i><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[→ <b>Zoey ‘Zo’ ‘Z’ ‘Zoeybird’ <s>Montgomery</s> Redbird</b> (16), main character. Zoey's life is turned upside down when she's Marked by a vampyre Tracker; she must transfer to the House of Night or her body will reject the Change and die. Her mark is filled, which is not normal for a fledging and she has affinities for all five elements: Air, Fire Water, Earth and Spirit, which has never happened before.<br>→ <b>Heath Luck</b> (17/18?), a football jock (quarterback) and Zoey's almost-ex-boyfriend who doesn't get the meaning of ‘‘it's over’’.<br>→ <b>Nyx</b>, the Goddess of Night and the personification of Night. She is known by many names including Changing Woman, Gaea, the name of the Earth Mother, Kuan Yin, Grandmother Spider, Dawn, A'akuluujjusi, and Nyx-Sekhmet. There are temples dedicated to her in every House of Night. Vampyres also honor her by living in a matriarchal society, where women have the rule, but men are honored and respected as guardians and companions and consorts. Nyx gives her children many gifts and once she has given a fledgling or vampyre an affinity, she never takes it back. Those who are given such abilities often excel in society, becoming High Priestesses or Warriors. Nyx's greatest gift for her children is free will, as she often says herself. <b>Erebus</b>, Nyx's consort.<br>→ <b>Sylvia Redbird</b>, Zoey's grandmother who's her only family support. Zoey's step-father and her mother doesn't accept her for who she is, leaving her to rely on her friends and grandmother. She lived on a lavender farm.<br>→ <b>Neferet</b>, the High Priestess of the Tulsa House of Night who acts as Zoey's mentor. <b>Skylar</b>, her cat? She has an affinity for their felines (cats), abilities as a healer, and she's also an intuitive - she can pick up bits and pieces of things.<br>→ <b>Aphrodite LaFont</b> (fourth former class? 17/18/19?), the snotty leader of The Dark Daughters and Son's whos gift from Nyx is visions of the future. She is Erik Night's ex-girlfriend. Neferet was her mentor.<br>→ <b>Stevie Rae Johnson</b> (third former class? 16/17?), the roommate and becomes Zoey's best friend who was Marked three months before her.<br>→ <b>Erik Night</b> (fifth former class? 18/19?), the hottest guy at the Tulsa House of Night and Zoey's crush.<br>→ <b>Erin Bates</b> (fourth former class? 17/18?), one half of the Twin Duo, becomes Zoey's friend.<br>→ <b>Shaunee Cole</b> (fourth former class? 17/18?), the other half - and roommate - of Erin Bates , becomes Zoey's friend. First, Shaunee and Erin call each other Twin because even though they are clearly not related—Erin being an extremely white girl from Tulsa, and Shaunee being of Jamaican descent and a lovely mocha color from Connecticut—they are freakishly alike. <b>Beelzebub</b> a cat that belongs to Erin and Shaunee; he chose both of them—together.<br>→ <b>Damien Maslin</b> (third former class? 16/17?), the gay friend of Zoey's new group of friend. <b>Cameron</b>, Damien’s cat.<br>→ <b>Kayla ‘K’ Robinson</b>, Zoey's former best friend from Broken Arrow, who kissed Zoey's then boyfriend Heath when they were sorta together.<br>→ <b>Linda Heffer</b>, Zoey's mom and wife to <b>John ‘step-loser’ Heffer</b>. She and Zoey had a falling out after she married John three years ago. He was an Elder of the People of Faith, a position he was oh, so proud of. <br>→ <b>Kevin ‘Troll’ Heffer</b>, Zoey's younger brother. Zoey also got an older sister but never mentions name. <br>→ Professor <b>Dragon Lankford</b> the Fencing Instructor.<br>→ Professor <b>Anastasia Lankford</b>, Dragon's wife and the Spells and Rituals, teacher.<br>→ Professor <b>Garmy</b> the Spanish teacher.<br>→ Professor <b>Penthesilia</b> the Literature teacher.<br>→ Professor <b>Nolan</b> the Drama teacher.<br>→ <b>Loren Blake</b> the Vamp Poet Laureate. He’s the first male Poet Laureate in two hundred years. And he’s only twenty-something real years, not just in looks.<br>→ <b>Lenobia</b>, the Equestrian Studies teacher.<br>→ <b>Nala</b>, Zoey's grumpy kitty.<br>→ <b>Elliott</b>, a young fledgling who's body rejects the Change, and dies. Zoey sees what she thinks is his ghost later on. Nala attacks this ghost, leading to Zoey questioning the ghost theory.<br>→ <b>Elizabeth No Last Name</b> is another young fledgling who's body rejects the Change, dies. Zoey sees what she thinks is her ghost after her death. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b><u>Quick basic facts</u>:</b><br><b>Genre</b>: - (Young Adult) Paranormal Romance.<br><b>Series</b>: - Series, Book One.<br><b>Love triangle?</b> - <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[No. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><b>Cheating?</b> - <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[No. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><b>HEA?</b> - <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[No. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><b>Favorite character?</b> - Nala?<br><b>Would I read more by this author/or of series?</b> - Sure.<br><b>Would I recommend this book/series?</b> - Sure, for those who like YA.<br><b>Will I read this again in the future?</b> - Probably not?<br><b>New Rating</b> - 3 stars.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445268775i/16623124.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>

<div id="review_518122073" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/518122073" />
    <a title="Mizuki" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16842102-mizuki"><img alt="Mizuki" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1368277474p2/16842102.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/518122073?book_show_action=true">Jan 26, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mizuki" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mizuki" href="/user/show/16842102-mizuki">Mizuki</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer518122073" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8892964289202718384">House of Night Book 1 Marked (by P C. Cast and Kristine Cast)<br/><br/>The story deals with the transformation of a human teenage girl Zoey Redbird into a vampyre fledgling. Zoey had her troubles at home, and her human friends more or less thought she'd turned into a monster when she was Marked and started changing into a vampyre. The girl seeked refuge in the House of Night, a high school for fledgling vampyres. In her new school Zoey struggled to adjust into her new life, she made friends with other fle</span>
  <span id="freeText8892964289202718384" style="display:none">House of Night Book 1 Marked (by P C. Cast and Kristine Cast)<br /><br />The story deals with the transformation of a human teenage girl Zoey Redbird into a vampyre fledgling. Zoey had her troubles at home, and her human friends more or less thought she'd turned into a monster when she was Marked and started changing into a vampyre. The girl seeked refuge in the House of Night, a high school for fledgling vampyres. In her new school Zoey struggled to adjust into her new life, she made friends with other fledglings and earned herself a few enemies, among them your typical queen bee Aphrodite, the leader of the Dark Daughters (a students' union of a sort) and the future High Priestess.<br /><br />The story should have been a lot of fun. But I can't help noticing that something is missing. In the world of House of Night, the existence of vampries seems to be more or less acknowledged and tolerated (at least it seems to be the case in America and Europe), but how and why the existence of vampires is tolerated? For how long things had been this way between humans and vampires? 10 years? 20 years or 100 years? Had the vampyres recently been 'Coming Out of the Coffin' like the vampires did in the Southern Vampires Mysteries series, or were they being acknowledged in an earlier time than that? None of the detail had ever been mentioned. I don't know whether P C. Cast and Kristine Cast had decided to save such key information for the latter books, but with those details missing, the whole story is narrowed down into the vampire high school and what happened inside the school. The outside world seems to be more or less ignored.<br /><br />Marked is the first book of the series and that's why I found the lack of world-building and supply of background information kind of shocking. Instead of some world-building, the authors only busy themselves to introduce the different aspects of the vampires world (e.g. the customs, the belief of the Goddess Nyx, mention of random historical/mythical figures who were vampyres, the function of the school...etc), without much explanation on...basically everything. We are given hardly anything else to understand Casts' world of vampire and human better. The authors only gave us the idea of what the vampires are like in the book, but hardly enlighten us with the reason why those vampires are what they are now. That's a bit disappointing.<br /><br />I also failed to understand why the Goddess Nyx, with all her wisdom would decide to gift Zoey with all five of the elemental powers. Why not give Zoey one or two powers for starter and let the girl earn more special abilities through hard work and chance? It looks really unnatural and wish-fulfilling when the main character's ability is a given, not something that she has to earn and improve with effort. You know even Harry Potter and co. had to study and practice so their magical abilities can develop further. *sighs*<br /><br />To sum up, Marked is entertaining enough, good for some time-killing but you won't find anything enlightening in it. My suggestion is, get the books from the library and read it for free. I won't spend a penny for the series, it doesn't worth my hard earned money.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8892964289202718384" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

           <span class="uitext reviewText">Mature teens</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to UniquelyMoi ~ BlithelyBookish by: </span>
      I saw this series at the bookstore and decided to check it out.

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish?shelf=own-have-read">own-have-read</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer33973777" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15753239944234514786"><br/>A very easy read. I wasn't sure if I wanted to read this book, but the first sentence, "Just when I thought my day couldn't get any worse, I saw the dead guy standing next to my locker.", got my attention.<br/><br/>The House of Night Series is yet another addition to the vampire/vampyre genre. Veering off of the traditional vampire path, in this series, vampyres are chosen and Marked, not Changed by being bitten, and not all those who have been Marked actually live through the Change. <br/><br/>In Marked, the first</span>
  <span id="freeText15753239944234514786" style="display:none"><br />A very easy read. I wasn't sure if I wanted to read this book, but the first sentence, "Just when I thought my day couldn't get any worse, I saw the dead guy standing next to my locker.", got my attention.<br /><br />The House of Night Series is yet another addition to the vampire/vampyre genre. Veering off of the traditional vampire path, in this series, vampyres are chosen and Marked, not Changed by being bitten, and not all those who have been Marked actually live through the Change. <br /><br />In Marked, the first book in the series, 16 year old Zoey Redbird is Marked by a vampyre Tracker and becomes a fledgling vampyre. She goes off to vampyre training school where she learns that she stands out as "special" among all the other fledglings there. In many ways it's a typical high school drama type story with the predictable characters. However there are enough twists and turns to make the story interesting.<br /><br />Just a couple 'heads up' because some people will find this offensive and because it's a young adult novel I wouldn't want any parents allowing their kids to read this based on my review without pointing out the following:<br /><br />1. The "f" word is salt and peppered throughout the book.<br /><br />2. By chapter 7, Zoey stumbles upon a scene she wishes she hadn't. Aphrodite, the school's High Priestess in training is desperately trying to convince Erik, an absolutely gorgeous upperclassman, that he really does want her to give him a "blow job." It was slightly explicit, and was something that was discussed in casual conversation a few times throughout the book. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15753239944234514786" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer46340823" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5896107365326169006">This book was recommended to me by my niece. I got her started with vampire books sometime back with Charlaine Harris' Sookie Stackhouse books. And I was the one who introduced her to Twilight. She gave me one of Richelle Mead's Vampire Academy books & I liked it, so figured this series might be okay, too. WRONG!! Others have mentioned the preponderance of pop culture references, which was annoying. However, my main quibbles are with Zoey's "perfectness" and what seemed to me to be a major "Chri</span>
  <span id="freeText5896107365326169006" style="display:none">This book was recommended to me by my niece. I got her started with vampire books sometime back with Charlaine Harris' Sookie Stackhouse books. And I was the one who introduced her to Twilight. She gave me one of Richelle Mead's Vampire Academy books &amp; I liked it, so figured this series might be okay, too. WRONG!! Others have mentioned the preponderance of pop culture references, which was annoying. However, my main quibbles are with Zoey's "perfectness" and what seemed to me to be a major "Christian bashing". I am not a religious person, but I do believe in God and this book seemed to paint all "People of Faith", as they were referred to in the book, with the "evil-stupid-intolerant" brush. While basically preaching a tolerance of everything else, the "People of Faith" were excluded. Add to this the fact that all the characters seemed terribly one dimensional and the "twins" were a couple of the most annoying characters I've come across in some time, you can be sure I won't bother with any of the others in this series.</span>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('+shBmHDzsM8z1L/+ZaEqw9nV7psBNnQDzPcqqVTNHonA7ihKy615p5T/C5+SVCAcD4oJU8+7+mSXiWwYmY7sEw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ph4whQWehKL0KKOLQqiUmq8XQzY2zAC5mXYoPOkvfBecOFlXvsBNylMDF+q1XZ5FeUik/vhBjt7CCG6NJGyOjQ==')})
  }
//]]>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer238144332285004412">PC was born in the Midwest, and grew up being shuttled back-and-forth between Illinois and Oklahoma, which is where she fell in love with Quarter Horses and mythology (at about the same time). After high school, she joined the United States Air Force and began public speaking and writing. After her tour in the USAF, she taught high school for 15 years before retiring to write full time. PC is a #1</span>
  <span id="freeText238144332285004412" style="display:none">PC was born in the Midwest, and grew up being shuttled back-and-forth between Illinois and Oklahoma, which is where she fell in love with Quarter Horses and mythology (at about the same time). After high school, she joined the United States Air Force and began public speaking and writing. After her tour in the USAF, she taught high school for 15 years before retiring to write full time. PC is a #1 New York Times and #1 USA Today Best-Selling author and a member of the Oklahoma Writers Hall of Fame. Her novels have been awarded the prestigious: Oklahoma Book Award, YALSA Quick Pick for Reluctant Readers, Romantic Times Reviewers’ Choice Award, the Prism, Holt Medallion, Daphne du Maurier, Booksellers’ Best, and the Laurel Wreath. PC is an experienced teacher and talented speaker. Ms. Cast lives in Oregon near her fabulous daughter, her adorable pack of dogs, her crazy Maine Coon, and a bunch of horses. House of Night Other World, book 4, FOUND, releases July 7th, 2020. More info to come soon about the HoN TV series! </span>
